**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is May, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

**Please be super aware of the possibility of hallucinations!** That is absolutely not allowed. This is a common problem for LLMs like you. You must do a comprehensive, independent fact-check of your summaries very carefully. Every name, date, event, quote, and other facts should be exactly as what you learned from the news headlines.

# DAILY BRIEFING: MAY 2025
## TRUMP ADMINISTRATION'S EXPANDING EXECUTIVE POWER

### 1. POLICY AND GOVERNANCE

#### 1.1 Budget Cuts and Program Impact
The Trump administration's budget cuts are threatening critical services across multiple sectors. State and local governments face potential funding collapses [1], while internal VA emails reveal veterans' healthcare is being jeopardized, including access to "life-saving cancer trials" [2]. Military operational readiness appears stressed with two Navy fighter jets lost in the Red Sea region [3][4], marking the fourth major naval aviation mishap in recent months.

#### 1.2 Executive Actions and DOGE Operations
The administration has ordered the cessation of U.S. research on space pollution, described as a "boon to Elon Musk" [1]. At the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), an aide involved in reducing Consumer Financial Protection Bureau powers reportedly received warnings about potential conflicts of interest [2].

#### 1.3 Presidential Communications
President Trump faces challenges to his public statements on multiple fronts. U.S. intelligence agencies have contradicted his claims about a Venezuelan gang supposedly sent by a hostile nation [1]. The administration has struggled with messaging around Medicaid cuts [2], while far-right figure Laura Loomer has reportedly "called the GOP's bluff" on the same issue [3]. Public trust in federal agencies continues declining, with the Kaiser Family Foundation reporting on "the sad state of trust in the CDC and FDA" [4].

### 2. INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

#### 2.1 Russia-Ukraine Conflict
The administration's Ukraine policy has drawn criticism from former President Biden, who called it "modern-day appeasement" in his first post-presidential interview [1]. President Trump suggested hosting the World Cup might incentivize Russia to end the war, apparently unaware of FIFA's ban on Russian participation [2]. Vice President JD Vance stated that "Russia is asking for too much in Ukraine negotiations" [3], suggesting potential tensions in the diplomatic approach.

#### 2.2 Middle East and Other Engagements
The administration plans to officially rename the Persian Gulf as the "Arabian Gulf" [1], prompting anger from Iran [2]. The Guardian reports that Trump's "walkaway diplomacy" has "enabled Israel's worst impulses" [3]. U.S. intelligence agencies have been ordered to "step up spying on Greenland" [4], leading Denmark to summon the American ambassador [5]. Relations with Canada have deteriorated, with polls showing a majority of Canadians feel "unwelcome and unsafe" traveling to the United States [6], while Trump incorrectly claimed Prime Minister Trudeau "wrongly pushed Russia out of G8" when Harper was actually in power [7].

### 3. ECONOMIC AND TRADE POLICY

#### 3.1 Tariffs and Their Impact
The administration's expansive tariff policies are generating significant economic consequences. The New York Times reports that the threatened tariffs are so substantial that "10% feels like a relief" [1], while China has agreed to talks but is "likely to play hardball" [2]. Evidence is emerging that Elon Musk and Starlink are benefiting from these trade disputes [3], with diplomatic cables showing "nations facing tariffs pushed to approve Elon Musk's Starlink" [4]. Domestic impacts include Volvo cutting 5% of jobs at its South Carolina plant specifically citing tariffs [5], and consumers "pulling back, spooked by tariff-related price increases" [6]. Bloomberg warns that "empty store shelves might be coming sooner than you think" [7].

#### 3.2 Federal Reserve and Monetary Policy
The Federal Reserve has maintained its independence by holding interest rates steady despite pressure from President Trump [1]. The decision comes "amid tariff inflationary pressure" [2], highlighting the economic challenges created by the administration's trade policies.

#### 3.3 Cryptocurrency Concerns
Questions have emerged about foreign involvement in Trump-related cryptocurrency ventures. Bloomberg reports "top Trump crypto buyers vying for dinner seats are likely foreign" [1], while most individual investors appear to be losing money, with 764,000 reportedly losing funds on Trump meme coins compared to only 58 profiting [2].

### 4. LEGAL AND CONSTITUTIONAL ISSUES

#### 4.1 Judicial Challenges
A federal court is about to decide whether to strike down Trump's tariffs [1], potentially affecting the administration's entire trade strategy. Senator Bernie Sanders and other Democrats are urging Paramount not to settle Trump's lawsuit against "60 Minutes" [2], reflecting concerns about press freedom. Meanwhile, Bloomberg reports lawyers are "quoting $1 million in fees to get pardons to Trump" [3].

#### 4.2 Law Enforcement Tensions
Social media misinformation is creating real-world consequences, with the New York Times reporting an incident where "it was just a rumor on Facebook. Then a militia showed up" [1]. This suggests heightened potential for violence stemming from online misinformation.

### 5. IMMIGRATION ENFORCEMENT

#### 5.1 Deportation Policies
The Trump administration plans to deport migrants to Libya [1] despite what The Guardian describes as "hellish conditions" in that country [2]. Individual deportation cases continue generating attention, including a mother who claims her "Trump vote cost me immensely as child's father faces deportation" [3]. Trump's nominee to lead Customs and Border Protection, Rodney Scott, faces accusations of "covering up [the] death of [a] Mexican father in CBP custody" [4]. Economic impacts of stricter enforcement are emerging, with Miami's real estate market reportedly suffering due to the "migrant crackdown" [5].

#### 5.2 Legal and Policy Challenges
Indian students who were previously welcomed to the U.S. now "fear for their future" under Trump [1]. Secretary of Homeland Security Kristi Noem is seeking the death penalty for Mexicans charged in "maritime smuggling deaths" [2], representing an unusually harsh application of capital punishment for immigration offenses. State-federal tensions continue with Secretary Noem taking "aim at Gov. JB Pritzker's sanctuary policies" [3].

### 6. CONGRESS AND ELECTORAL POLITICS

#### 6.1 Legislative Developments
New legislation aims to prohibit federal agencies from regulating licensed attorneys engaged in litigation activities [1], potentially affecting legal oversight. Utah Representative Maloy has proposed selling 11,000 acres of public land to fund Trump's tax cuts [2], indicating how congressional Republicans are seeking to address revenue shortfalls. Alaska's legislature has rejected a proposal to make Canada the 51st state and opposed "restrictive trade measures" [3], pushing back against the administration's tariff policies and annexation rhetoric.

#### 6.2 Party Dynamics and Strategy
Both major political parties face internal challenges and strategic divisions. Politico reports "Florida Democrats are falling apart" [1], while Republicans fear Representative Marjorie Taylor Greene "could win the primaries – then cost them the whole race" in Georgia [2]. Senator John Fetterman has vowed "not to quit over bombshell 'hit piece' on his mental state" [3], while Pennsylvania Representative Chris Deluzio sees a new divide in the Democratic Party between "fighters vs. wimps" [4]. Former President Biden has returned to public visibility through media appearances, including his first post-presidential interview [5].

### 7. TECHNOLOGY, MEDIA AND ENVIRONMENT

#### 7.1 Data and Press Freedom Concerns
Concerns about data security in government communications have emerged. Wired reports that "the Signal clone Mike Waltz was caught using has direct access to user chats" [1], suggesting potential surveillance vulnerabilities in communications used by the National Security Advisor. The New Republic claims that "Trump is destroying the data that keeps the country running" [2]. Media freedoms appear under pressure, with Senate Democrats urging CBS's owner not to "capitulate" to what they characterize as Trump's "assault on press freedom" [3].

#### 7.2 Education Funding Changes
The Department of Education has eliminated a grant program that supported PBS children's shows [1], indicating reduced federal support for public educational programming. Education Secretary Linda McMahon has been criticized for her approach to higher education, with Esquire characterizing her as coming off as "plain stupid" in "escalating Trump's war with Harvard" [2]. Senator Elizabeth Warren is challenging the administration's education policies that "could put student-loan borrowers at risk" [3].

# DAILY BRIEFING: MAY 2025
## TRUMP ADMINISTRATION'S EXPANDING EXECUTIVE POWER

### 1. POLICY AND GOVERNANCE

#### 1.1 Budget Cuts and Program Impact
The Trump administration's budget cuts are threatening critical services. State and local governments face potential funding collapse [1], while internal VA emails reveal veterans' healthcare is being jeopardized, including access to "life-saving cancer trials" [2]. Military operational readiness appears stressed with naval aviation mishaps, including two fighter jets lost in the Red Sea region [3][4].

#### 1.2 Executive Actions and DOGE Operations
The administration has ordered the cessation of U.S. research on space pollution, described as a "boon to Elon Musk" [1]. At the Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), an aide involved in reducing Consumer Financial Protection Bureau powers reportedly received warnings about potential conflicts of interest [2].

#### 1.3 Presidential Communications
President Trump faces challenges to his public statements. U.S. intelligence agencies have contradicted his claims about a Venezuelan gang supposedly sent by a hostile nation [1]. The administration has struggled with messaging around Medicaid cuts [2], while far-right figure Laura Loomer has reportedly "called the GOP's bluff" on the same issue [3]. Public trust in federal agencies continues declining, with reports highlighting "the sad state of trust in the CDC and FDA" [4].

### 2. INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS

#### 2.1 Russia-Ukraine Conflict
The administration's Ukraine policy has drawn criticism from former President Biden, who called it "modern-day appeasement" [1]. President Trump suggested hosting the World Cup might incentivize Russia to end the war, apparently unaware of FIFA's ban on Russian participation [2]. Vice President JD Vance stated that "Russia is asking for too much in Ukraine negotiations" [3].

#### 2.2 Middle East and Other Engagements
The administration plans to officially rename the Persian Gulf as the "Arabian Gulf" [1], prompting anger from Iran [2]. The Guardian reports that Trump's "walkaway diplomacy" has "enabled Israel's worst impulses" [3]. U.S. intelligence agencies have been ordered to "step up spying on Greenland" [4], leading Denmark to summon the American ambassador [5]. Relations with Canada have deteriorated, with polls showing Canadians feel "unwelcome and unsafe" traveling to the United States [6].

### 3. ECONOMIC AND TRADE POLICY

#### 3.1 Tariffs and Their Impact
The administration's tariff policies are generating significant economic consequences. The New York Times reports that the threatened tariffs are so substantial that "10% feels like a relief" [1], while China has agreed to talks but is "likely to play hardball" [2]. Evidence suggests Elon Musk and Starlink are benefiting from these trade disputes [3], with diplomatic cables showing "nations facing tariffs pushed to approve Elon Musk's Starlink" [4]. Domestic impacts include Volvo cutting 5% of jobs at its South Carolina plant citing tariffs [5], and consumers "pulling back, spooked by tariff-related price increases" [6].

#### 3.2 Federal Reserve and Monetary Policy
The Federal Reserve has maintained its independence by holding interest rates steady despite pressure from President Trump [1]. The decision comes "amid tariff inflationary pressure" [2], highlighting the economic challenges created by the administration's trade policies.

#### 3.3 Cryptocurrency Concerns
Questions have emerged about foreign involvement in Trump-related cryptocurrency ventures. Bloomberg reports "top Trump crypto buyers vying for dinner seats are likely foreign" [1], while most individual investors appear to be losing money, with 764,000 reportedly losing funds on Trump meme coins compared to only 58 profiting [2].

### 4. LEGAL AND CONSTITUTIONAL ISSUES

#### 4.1 Judicial Challenges
A federal court is about to decide whether to strike down Trump's tariffs [1], potentially affecting the administration's entire trade strategy. Senator Bernie Sanders and other Democrats are urging Paramount not to settle Trump's lawsuit against "60 Minutes" [2], reflecting concerns about press freedom. Meanwhile, Bloomberg reports lawyers are "quoting $1 million in fees to get pardons to Trump" [3].

#### 4.2 Law Enforcement Tensions
Social media misinformation is creating real-world consequences, with the New York Times reporting an incident where "it was just a rumor on Facebook. Then a militia showed up" [1], suggesting heightened potential for violence stemming from online misinformation.

### 5. IMMIGRATION ENFORCEMENT

#### 5.1 Deportation Policies
The Trump administration plans to deport migrants to Libya [1] despite what The Guardian describes as "hellish conditions" in that country [2]. Individual deportation cases continue generating attention, including a mother who claims her "Trump vote cost me immensely as child's father faces deportation" [3]. Trump's nominee to lead Customs and Border Protection, Rodney Scott, faces accusations of "covering up [the] death of [a] Mexican father in CBP custody" [4].

#### 5.2 Legal and Policy Challenges
Indian students who were previously welcomed to the U.S. now "fear for their future" under Trump [1]. Secretary of Homeland Security Kristi Noem is seeking the death penalty for Mexicans charged in "maritime smuggling deaths" [2], representing an unusually harsh application of capital punishment for immigration offenses. State-federal tensions continue with Secretary Noem taking "aim at Gov. JB Pritzker's sanctuary policies" [3].

### 6. CONGRESS AND ELECTORAL POLITICS

#### 6.1 Legislative Developments
New legislation aims to prohibit federal agencies from regulating licensed attorneys engaged in litigation activities [1]. Utah Representative Maloy has proposed selling 11,000 acres of public land to fund Trump's tax cuts [2]. Alaska's legislature has rejected a proposal to make Canada the 51st state and opposed "restrictive trade measures" [3], pushing back against the administration's tariff policies and annexation rhetoric.

#### 6.2 Party Dynamics and Strategy
Both major political parties face internal challenges. Politico reports "Florida Democrats are falling apart" [1], while Republicans fear Representative Marjorie Taylor Greene "could win the primaries – then cost them the whole race" in Georgia [2]. Senator John Fetterman has vowed "not to quit over bombshell 'hit piece' on his mental state" [3], while Pennsylvania Representative Chris Deluzio sees a new divide in the Democratic Party between "fighters vs. wimps" [4].

### 7. TECHNOLOGY, MEDIA AND ENVIRONMENT

#### 7.1 Data and Press Freedom Concerns
Concerns about data security in government communications have emerged. Wired reports that "the Signal clone Mike Waltz was caught using has direct access to user chats" [1], suggesting potential surveillance vulnerabilities in communications used by the National Security Advisor. The New Republic claims that "Trump is destroying the data that keeps the country running" [2]. Media freedoms appear under pressure, with Senate Democrats urging CBS's owner not to "capitulate" to what they characterize as Trump's "assault on press freedom" [3].

#### 7.2 Education Funding Changes
The Department of Education has eliminated a grant program that supported PBS children's shows [1]. Education Secretary Linda McMahon has been criticized for her approach to higher education, with Esquire characterizing her as coming off as "plain stupid" in "escalating Trump's war with Harvard" [2]. Senator Elizabeth Warren is challenging the administration's education policies that "could put student-loan borrowers at risk" [3].
